2:34:2453:0:14:72:219:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:Financial Intermediary Capital
2:35:2483:14:14:72:269:686:12:Times:12:Times:?:Adriano A. Rampini and S. Viswanathan
2:36:2520:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 23302
2:37:2548:14:14:72:130:658:12:Times:12:Times:?:March 2017
2:38:2558:14:28:72:250:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. E02,E32,E51,G01,G21,G32
2:39:2589:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:A:ABSTRACT
2:40:2597:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:?:We  propose  a  dynamic  theory  of  financial  intermediaries  that  are  better  able  to  collateralize 
2:41:2704:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:claims than households, that is, have a collateralization advantage. Intermediaries require capital 
2:42:2803:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:as  they  can borrow  against  their  loans  only  to  the  extent  that  households  themselves  can 
2:43:2904:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:collateralize  the  assets backing  these  loans.  The  net  worth  of  financial  intermediaries  and  the 
2:44:3011:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:corporate  sector  are  both  state variables  affecting  the  spread  between  intermediated  and  direct 
2:45:3117:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:finance  and  the  dynamics  of  real  economic activity,  such  as  investment,  and  financing.  The 
2:46:3219:14:14:71:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:accumulation  of  net  worth  of  intermediaries  is  slow relative  to  that  of  the  corporate  sector.  The 
2:47:3330:14:14:71:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:model  is  consistent  with  key  stylized  facts  about  macroeconomic downturns  associated  with  a 
2:48:3432:14:14:71:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:credit  crunch,  namely,  their  severity,  their  protractedness,  and  the  fact that  the  severity  of  the 
2:49:3543:14:14:71:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:?:credit  crunch  itself  affects  the  severity  and  persistence  of  downturns.  The  model captures  the 
2:50:3649:14:42:71:327:448:12:Times:12:Times:?:tentative and halting nature of recoveries from crises.
2:51:3704:42:14:71:169:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:Adriano A. Rampini
2:52:3722:14:14:71:151:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:Duke University
2:53:3737:14:14:71:196:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:Fuqua School of Business
2:54:3761:14:14:71:152:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:100 Fuqua Drive

2:59:3829:14:14:72:152:280:12:Times:12:Times:?:Duke University
2:60:3844:14:14:72:197:266:12:Times:12:Times:?:Fuqua School of Business
2:61:3868:14:14:72:153:252:12:Times:12:Times:?:100 Fuqua Drive
2:62:3883:14:14:72:167:238:12:Times:12:Times:?:Durham, NC 27708
2:63:3899:14:14:72:124:224:12:Times:12:Times:?:and NBER

3:65:3924:0:29:80:216:699:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:66:3941:29:17:80:532:670:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The capitalization of financial intermediaries is arguably critical for economic fluctuations
3:67:4034:17:18:80:532:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and growth.  We provide a dynamic theory of financial intermediaries that have a collater-
3:68:4124:18:17:80:532:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:alization advantage, that is, are better able to collateralize claims than households.  Firms
3:69:4217:17:17:80:532:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:need to collateralize promises to pay with tangible assets and can raise collateralized fi-
3:70:4308:17:18:80:532:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nancing from both intermediaries and households;  firms require net worth as collateral
3:71:4395:18:17:80:532:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraints limit financing.  Financial intermediaries require net worth as their ability to
3:72:4487:17:17:80:532:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:refinance their collateralized loans from households is in turn limited, as they, too, need
3:73:4578:17:18:80:532:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to collateralize their promises.  Importantly,  the net worth of both financial intermedi-
3:74:4668:18:17:80:532:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aries and firms hence plays a role in our model, in contrast to most previous work, and
3:75:4755:17:17:80:532:514:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these two state variables jointly determine the dynamics of economic activity, investment,
3:76:4845:17:18:80:532:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing, and loan spreads.  A key feature of our model is that the accumulation of the
3:77:4933:18:17:80:532:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net  worth  of  intermediaries  is  slow  relative  to  that  of  the  corporate  sector.   The  slow-
3:78:5035:17:17:80:532:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:moving nature of intermediary capital results in economic dynamics that are consistent
3:79:5121:17:18:80:532:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with key stylized facts about macroeconomic downturns associated with a credit crunch,
3:80:5207:18:17:80:532:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:namely, their severity, their protractedness, and the fact that the severity of the credit
3:81:5297:17:18:80:532:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crunch itself affects the severity and persistence of downturns.  Most uniquely, the model
3:82:5387:18:17:80:420:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:captures the tentative and halting nature of recoveries from crises.
3:83:5455:17:17:98:533:375:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the model firms can borrow from both intermediaries and households, and all fi-
3:84:5537:17:18:80:532:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nancing needs to be collateralized.  Firm financing is subject to two types of collateral
3:85:5626:18:17:80:532:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraints, one for loans from households and one for loans from intermediaries.  Since
3:86:5714:17:17:80:532:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries are better able to enforce collateralized claims, they can lend more than
3:87:5802:17:18:80:532:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:households,  but  the  additional  amount  that  they  can  lend  has  to  be  financed  out  of
3:88:5898:18:17:80:532:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their own net worth, giving a role to financial intermediary capital.  We show that these
3:89:5987:17:17:80:532:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateral constraints can be derived from an economy with limited enforcement that con-
3:90:6075:17:18:80:532:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strains firms’ and intermediaries’ ability to make credible promises.  Intermediaries, but
3:91:6165:18:17:80:532:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not households, participate in markets at all times which affords intermediaries with an
3:92:6253:17:17:80:532:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advantage in enforcing claims.  This economy with limited enforcement without exclusion
3:93:6340:17:18:80:530:202:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:and with limited participation is equivalent to our economy with collateral constraints.1
3:94:6429:18:17:98:533:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Intermediaries  are  essential  in  our  economy  in  the  sense  that  allocations  can  be
3:95:6521:17:17:80:532:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:achieved  with  financial  intermediaries,  which  cannot  be  achieved  otherwise.   Since  in-
3:96:6617:17:18:80:532:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:termediary net worth is limited, intermediated finance commands a positive spread.  In a
3:97:6705:18:17:80:532:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deterministic steady state, the equilibrium capitalization of both the representative firm
3:98:6795:17:18:93:532:115:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:1We  model  limited  enforcement  `a  la  Kehoe  and  Levine  (1993)  but  without  exclusion,  as  in  Chien
3:99:6904:18:15:80:532:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and Lustig (2010) and Rampini and Viswanathan (2010, 2013), and extend their results by introducing
3:100:7003:15:0:80:205:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:limited participation as well.
4:101:7034:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and intermediary are positive.  Steady state firm net worth is determined by the fraction
4:102:7123:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of tangible assets that firms cannot pledge to intermediaries or households and thus have
4:103:7212:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to finance internally.  Steady state intermediary net worth is determined by the fraction
4:104:7301:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of investment that intermediaries have to finance due to their collateralization advantage,
4:105:7392:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that is, by the difference in the ability to enforce collateralized claims between interme-
4:106:7483:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diaries and households.  As an aside, the determinants of the capital structure for firms
4:107:7572:17:17:80:335:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and intermediaries are thus distinct in our model.
4:108:7622:17:18:98:533:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The equilibrium spread on intermediated finance is determined by the two state vari-
4:109:7706:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ables, firm and intermediary net worth, jointly.  Intermediary net worth increases inter-
4:110:7795:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediated  loan  supply  and  hence  reduces  spreads  all  else  equal.   In  contrast,  firm  net
4:111:7893:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth has two opposing effects on intermediated loan demand:  on the one hand, firm net
4:112:7980:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth increases investment and lowers the levered marginal product of capital reducing
4:113:8066:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms’ willingness to pay, lowering spreads; on the other hand, firm net worth, by increas-
4:114:8157:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing investment, increases firms’ collateralizable assets, which in turn raises loan demand,
4:115:8248:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:raising spreads.  Hence, spreads can be high or low when firm net worth is low as they
4:116:8334:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depend on the relative capitalization of firms and intermediaries.  When intermediary net
4:117:8423:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth is relatively scarce, the collateral constraint on intermediated finance is slack and
4:118:8514:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm net worth reduces spreads.  When firm net worth is relatively scarce instead, the col-
4:119:8605:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lateral constraint on intermediated finance binds and firm net worth increases spreads as
4:120:8694:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it increases firms’ ability to pledge and hence loan demand.  Notably, equilibrium spreads
4:121:8784:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be low in the model even when firms are poorly capitalized.  This interaction of loan
4:122:8873:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:supply and demand results in rich and subtle dynamics of intermediated finance and loan
4:123:8960:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads,  with  negative  shocks  to  net  worth  potentially  leading  to  spreads  dropping  on
4:124:9057:18:17:80:464:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impact, then spiking, and finally falling as the economy gradually recovers.
4:125:9133:17:17:98:533:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our model allows the analysis of the dynamics of the capitalization of the corporate
4:126:9217:17:18:80:532:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and intermediary sector.  The two state variables, net worth of firms and intermediaries,
4:127:9306:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:jointly determine the dynamic supply and demand for intermediated loans and the equi-
4:128:9391:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium interest rate.  A key feature of the equilibrium dynamics is that intermediary net
4:129:9481:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth accumulation is slow relative to corporate net worth accumulation.  This feature is
4:130:9570:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reflected in several aspects of the dynamics of the model.  First, the recovery from a credit
4:131:9663:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crunch, that is, a drop in intermediary net worth, is relatively slow making such episodes
4:132:9753:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:protracted. Second, the recovery from a downturn associated with a credit crunch, that is,
4:133:9843:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a drop in corporate and intermediary net worth, can stall, after an initial relatively swift
4:134:9935:17:17:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovery,  when firm net worth has partially recovered while intermediaries have yet to
4:135:10022:17:18:80:532:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recover.  Third, the recovery from a downturn associated with a more severe credit crunch
4:136:10111:18:0:80:532:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is especially slow and halting, with output depressed and spreads elevated for a prolonged
5:137:10202:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period of time.  The reason why intermediaries accumulate net worth more slowly in the
5:138:10288:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model is that their net worth grows at the intermediated interest rate, which is at most
5:139:10376:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the marginal levered product of capital, and may be lower than that when the collateral
5:140:10463:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraint on intermediated finance binds.  In contrast, firms accumulate net worth at the
5:141:10553:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average levered product of capital, which in turn exceeds the marginal levered product of
5:142:10642:18:17:80:118:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital.
5:143:10650:17:17:98:533:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a downturn without a credit crunch, that is, a drop in corporate net worth alone,
5:144:10734:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate investment drops; as a consequence of the collateral constraints on intermedi-
5:145:10822:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ated finance, corporate loan demand for intermediated loans drops as well, resulting in a
5:146:10911:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:drop in the intermediated interest rate.  Indeed, intermediaries find themselves temporar-
5:147:11001:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ily  relatively  well  capitalized  and  facing  reduced  loan  demand  respond  in  two  possible
5:148:11099:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ways.  On the one hand, intermediaries may lend some funds to households at an inter-
5:149:11184:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:est rate lower than that implied by their own rate of time preference, and in this sense
5:150:11272:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries  may  hold  “cash,”  to  conserve  net  worth  in  order  to  meet  higher  future
5:151:11369:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate loan demand.  Corporate loan demand is expected to recover relatively quickly
5:152:11456:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as  firms  reaccumulate  net  worth.   On  the  other  hand,  if  corporate  loan  demand  is  ex-
5:153:11554:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pected to remain depressed for an extended period of time, intermediaries may conserve
5:154:11640:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only part of their net worth and pay out some net worth as an initial dividend.  As firms
5:155:11729:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reaccumulate  net  worth,  corporate  loan  demand  rises,  and  intermediary  net  worth  be-
5:156:11823:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:comes scarce.  Initially, the intermediated interest rate rises as the collateral constraint
5:157:11915:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:still binds,  limiting loan demand.  Eventually,  the intermediated interest rate starts to
5:158:12006:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fall again, as firms accumulate sufficient net worth, so that the collateral constraint no
5:159:12096:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:longer binds, and intermediary loan supply becomes the limiting factor.  Firms initiate
5:160:12183:18:17:80:532:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dividends  even  before  the  economy  has  fully  recovered,  whereas  intermediaries  do  not
5:161:12278:17:17:80:325:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:resume payout until the steady state is reached.
5:162:12326:17:18:98:533:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a credit crunch, that is, a drop in intermediary net worth, investment drops even if
5:163:12413:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the corporate sector remains well capitalized, as firms need to finance a larger part of their
5:164:12507:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment with internal funds due to the limited supply of intermediated loans.  Indeed,
5:165:12596:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms are forced to delever and may temporarily accumulate more net worth then they
5:166:12679:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:retain in the steady state.  Moreover, and importantly, a credit crunch can have persistent
5:167:12770:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real effects as corporate investment may not recover for a prolonged period of time, due to
5:168:12861:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the slow recovery of intermediary capital.  We emphasize that while firms may seem to be
5:169:12949:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well capitalized because they are paying dividends, the economy nevertheless has not fully
5:170:13039:17:17:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovered.  Downturns associated with a credit crunch, that is, a drop in both corporate
5:171:13127:17:18:80:532:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and intermediary net worth, are more severe and more protracted, lead to longer stalls
5:172:13213:18:0:80:513:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the recovery, and feature higher spreads, especially in a bank-dependent economy.
6:173:13298:0:17:98:533:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We revisit the evidence on the effect of financial crises from the vantage point of our
6:174:13385:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:theory.   There  are  three  main  stylized  facts  about  downturns  associated  with  financial
6:175:13482:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crises that emerge from prior empirical work: (i) downturns associated with financial crises
6:176:13574:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are more severe; (ii) recoveries from financial crises are protracted and often tentative; and
6:177:13668:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(iii) the severity of the financial crises itself affects the severity and protractedness of the
6:178:13764:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:downturn.  Consistent with this evidence, our model predicts that the effects of a credit
6:179:13853:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crunch on economic activity is protracted due to the slow accumulation of intermediary
6:180:13939:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net  worth.   But  perhaps  most  uniquely,  our  model  captures  the  tentative  and  halting
6:181:14034:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nature of recoveries from such episodes emphasized by Reinhart and Rogoff (2014) and
6:182:14118:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allows the analysis of the severity of the credit crunch itself on the recovery, which calls
6:183:14210:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  a  model  with  two  state  variables.   Thus,  the  dynamic  interaction  of  the  two  state
6:184:14309:18:17:80:491:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables in our model implies rich dynamics with empirically plausible features.
6:185:14390:17:17:98:533:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Few extant theories of financial intermediaries provide a role for intermediary capi-
6:186:14475:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tal.  Notable is in particular Holmstr ̈om and Tirole (1997) who model intermediaries as
6:187:14563:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monitors that cannot commit to monitoring and hence need to have their own capital at
6:188:14648:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stake to have incentives to monitor.  In their analysis, firm and intermediary capital are
6:189:14738:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exogenous and the comparative statics with respect to these are analyzed.  Holmstr ̈om
6:190:14824:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Tirole conclude that “[a] proper investigation ...  must take into account the feed-
6:191:14912:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:back from interest rates to capital values.  This will require an explicitly dynamic model,
6:192:15003:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  instance,  along  the  lines  of  Kiyotaki  and  Moore  [1997a].”   We  provide  a  dynamic
6:193:15099:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model in which the joint evolution of firm and intermediary net worth and the interest
6:194:15185:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate on intermediated finance are endogenously determined.  Diamond and Rajan (2001)
6:195:15269:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Diamond  (2007)  model  intermediaries  as  lenders  which  are  better  able  to  enforce
6:196:15364:18:17:80:532:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their claims due to their specific liquidation or monitoring ability in a similar spirit to
6:197:15455:17:17:80:532:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our model, but do not consider equilibrium dynamics.  In contrast, the capitalization of
6:198:15543:17:18:80:532:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial intermediaries plays essentially no role in liquidity provision theories of finan-
6:199:15635:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cial intermediation (Diamond and Dybvig (1983)), in theories of financial intermediaries
6:200:15723:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as delegated, diversified monitors (Diamond (1984), Ramakrishnan and Thakor (1984),
6:201:15806:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Williamson (1986)) or in coalition based theories (Townsend (1978) and Boyd and
6:202:15889:18:17:80:167:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Prescott (1986)).
6:203:15906:17:17:98:533:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Dynamic models in which net worth plays a role, such as Bernanke and Gertler (1989)
6:204:15989:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Kiyotaki and Moore (1997a), typically consider the role of firm net worth only, al-
6:205:16076:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:though  dynamic  models  in  which  intermediary  net  worth  matters  have  recently  been
6:206:16167:17:17:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considered (see, for example, Gertler and Kiyotaki (2010), who also summarize the recent
6:207:16255:17:19:80:532:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literature, and Brunnermeier and Sannikov (2014)).2However, to the best of our knowl-
6:208:16340:19:0:93:532:91:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:2Gromb and Vayanos (2002) and He and Krishnamurthy (2012) study the asset pricing implications
7:209:16435:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:edge, we are the first to consider a dynamic contracting model in which both firm and
7:210:16520:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediary net worth are critical and jointly affect the dynamics of financing, spreads,
7:211:16610:18:17:80:194:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and economic activity.
7:212:16632:17:17:98:533:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In Section 2 we describe the model with two types of collateral constraints,  for in-
7:213:16717:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:termediated and direct finance, respectively, and discuss how these collateral constraints
7:214:16807:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be derived in an economy with limited enforcement and limited participation.  We
7:215:16891:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:establish the equivalence of these two economies formally in Appendix A. Section 3 shows
7:216:16979:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that intermediation is essential in our economy and determines the capitalization of in-
7:217:17067:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:termediaries  and  spreads  on  intermediated  finance  in  the  steady  state.   The  dynamics
7:218:17162:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of intermediary capital are analyzed in Section 4,  focusing on the dynamic interaction
7:219:17249:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between  corporate  and  intermediary  net  worth,  the  two  state  variables  in  the  model;
7:220:17344:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specifically, we consider the effects of a downturn, a credit crunch, and a downturn asso-
7:221:17434:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ciated with a credit crunch.  In Section 5 we use the model to revisit three main stylized
7:222:17524:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:facts about downturns associated with financial crises.  Section 6 concludes.  All proofs
7:223:17613:18:44:80:178:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are in Appendix B.
7:224:17631:44:29:80:465:412:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Collateralized finance with intermediation
7:225:17678:29:17:80:532:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  propose  a  dynamic  model  of  financial  intermediaries  that  have  a  collateralization
7:226:17773:17:18:80:532:366:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advantage, that is, are better able to collateralize claims than households.  In the model
7:227:17863:18:17:80:532:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms can borrow from both intermediaries and households, and all financing needs to be
7:228:17950:17:17:80:532:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateralized.   Firm  financing  is  subject  to  two  types  of  collateral  constraints,  one  for
7:229:18052:17:18:80:532:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:loans  from  households  and  one  for  loans  from  intermediaries.   Since  intermediaries  are
7:230:18149:18:17:80:532:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:better able to enforce collateralized claims, they can lend more than households, but the
7:231:18238:17:17:80:532:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:additional  amount  that  they  can  lend  has  to  be  financed  out  of  their  own  net  worth,
7:232:18336:17:18:80:532:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:giving a role to financial intermediary capital.  Thus, the net worth of both intermediaries
7:233:18428:18:17:80:435:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and firms are state variables and jointly determine economic activity.
7:234:18498:17:18:98:533:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We show that these collateral constraints can be derived from an economy with limited
7:235:18583:18:17:80:532:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enforcement that constrains firms’ and intermediaries’ ability to make credible promises.
7:236:18672:17:17:80:532:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intermediaries, but not households, participate in markets at all times which affords inter-
7:237:18764:17:18:80:532:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediaries with an advantage in enforcing claims.  This economy with limited enforcement
7:238:18851:18:21:80:499:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and limited participation is equivalent to our economy with collateral constraints.
7:239:18934:21:0:80:280:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of intermediary net worth in dynamic models.
8:240:18979:0:25:80:208:699:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Environment
8:241:18997:25:17:80:532:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Time is discrete and the horizon infinite.  There are three types of agents:  entrepreneurs,
8:242:19089:17:18:80:417:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial intermediaries, and households; we discuss these in turn.
8:243:19156:18:17:98:533:639:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:There is a continuum of entrepreneurs or firms with measure one which are risk neutral
8:244:19242:17:17:80:532:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and subject to limited liability and discount the future at rateβ∈(0,1).  We consider an
8:245:19330:17:18:80:532:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:environment with a representative firm.  The representative firm (which we at times refer
8:246:19419:18:17:80:532:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to simply as the firm or the corporate sector) has limited net worthw0at time 0 and has
8:247:19506:17:17:80:532:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:access to a standard neoclassical production technology; an investment of an amountktof
8:248:19593:17:18:80:532:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital at timetyields outputA(st+1)f(kt) at timet+1 whereA(st+1)>0 is the stochastic
8:249:19678:18:17:80:532:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:total factor productivity andf(·) is the production function.  Capitalktdepreciates at
8:250:19764:17:17:80:532:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the rateδ∈(0,1).  We assume that the production functionf(·) is strictly increasing
8:251:19847:17:18:80:532:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and strictly concave and satisfies the usual Inada condition, that is, limk→0fk(k) = +∞.
8:252:19935:18:17:80:532:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Total factor productivityA(st+1) depends on the statest+1realized at timet+ 1 which
8:253:20018:17:17:80:532:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:follows a Markov process with transition function Π(st,st+1).  The firm can raise financing
8:254:20109:17:18:80:397:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from both intermediaries and households as we discuss below.
8:255:20169:18:17:98:533:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:There  is  a  continuum  of  financial  intermediaries  with  measure  one  which  are  risk
8:256:20261:17:17:80:533:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:neutral, subject to limited liability, and discount future payoffs atβi∈(0,1).  We consider
8:257:20352:17:18:80:532:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  problem  of  a  representative  financial  intermediary  with  limited  net  worthwi0at
8:258:20444:18:17:80:532:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time 0.3Intermediaries can lend to and borrow from firms and households as described
8:259:20528:17:17:80:188:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in more detail below.
8:260:20549:17:18:98:533:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:There  is  a  continuum  of  households  with  measure  one  which  are  risk  neutral  and
8:261:20640:18:17:80:532:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discount future payoffs at a rateR−1∈(0,1).  Households are assumed to have a large
8:262:20723:17:17:80:532:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endowment of funds and collateral in all dates and states, and hence are not subject to
8:263:20810:17:18:80:532:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enforcement problems but rather are able to commit to deliver on their promises.  They
8:264:20896:18:17:80:532:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are willing to provide any state-contingent claim at an expected rate of returnRas long
8:265:20983:17:17:80:457:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as such claims satisfy the firms’ and intermediaries’ collateral constraints.
8:266:21060:17:18:98:532:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We assume thatβ < βi< R−1, that is, households are more patient than intermedi-
8:267:21139:18:17:80:532:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aries which in turn are more patient than the firms.  Since firms and intermediaries are
8:268:21227:17:17:80:532:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financially constrained, they would have an incentive to accumulate net worth and save
8:269:21313:17:18:80:532:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:themselves out of their constraints.  Assuming that firms and intermediaries are impatient
8:270:21403:18:17:80:532:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative to households is a simple way to ensure that their net worth matters even in the
8:271:21492:17:17:80:532:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:long run.  Moreover, assuming that intermediaries are somewhat more patient than firms
8:272:21578:17:18:80:532:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that the net worth of both the corporate sector and the intermediary sector are
8:273:21665:18:18:93:532:119:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:3There is a representative intermediary in our model since intermediaries have constant returns to
8:274:21763:18:15:80:532:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:scale, making the distribution of intermediaries’ net worth irrelevant and aggregation in the intermedia-
8:275:21868:15:0:80:520:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:tion sector straightforward, and thus only the aggregate capital of the intermediation sector matters.
9:276:21971:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:uniquely determined in the long run, too.  We think these features are desirable properties
9:277:22062:17:18:80:427:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a dynamic model of intermediation and are empirically plausible.
9:278:22129:18:17:98:533:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Financial intermediaries in this economy have a collateralization advantage.  Specif-
9:279:22214:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically, intermediaries are better able to collateralize claims than households, that is, in-
9:280:22306:17:18:80:533:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:termediaries are able to seize up to fractionθi∈(0,1) of the (resale value of) collateral
9:281:22395:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:backing promises issued to them whereas households are able to seize only fractionθ < θi,
9:282:22484:17:17:80:164:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereθ∈(0,1).
9:283:22497:17:18:98:533:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One interpretation of the environment is that there are three types of capital, working
9:284:22584:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital,  equipment  (fractionθi−θ),  and  structures  (fractionθ)  (see  Figure  1).   Firms
9:285:22677:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have to finance working capital entirely out of their own net worth.  Only intermediaries
9:286:22766:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can  lend  against  equipment,  but  both  households  and  intermediaries  can  lend  against
9:287:22860:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:structures.  Equipment loans have to be extended by intermediaries and have to be finance
9:288:22949:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out of financial intermediary capital.  We refer to these loans as intermediated finance.
9:289:23038:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast, structure loans can be provided by either intermediaries or households.  We
9:290:23126:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assume  that  these  loans  are  provided  by  households  and  refer  to  such  loans  as  direct
9:291:23224:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance.   This  is  without  loss  of  generality  and  we  could  equivalently  assume  that  all
9:292:23323:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate loans are extended by the intermediary who in turn borrows from households,
9:293:23408:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which we refer to as theindirect implementation.  However, we focus on the (equivalent)
9:294:23495:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f3:B:direct implementationin which households extend all structure loans directly throughout
9:295:23582:17:18:80:294:370:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:as it simplifies the notation and analysis.4
9:296:23626:18:17:98:533:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  assume  that  loans  are  one-period  and  state-contingent  and  thus,  the  economy
9:297:23715:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has complete markets in two types of one-period ahead Arrow securities, claims provided
9:298:23802:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by intermediaries and claims provided by households, each subject to state-by-state col-
9:299:23890:18:17:80:532:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lateral constraints.  These collateral constraints are similar to the ones in Kiyotaki and
9:300:23980:17:17:80:532:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moore (1997a), except that there are different collateral constraints for promises to pay
9:301:24069:17:18:80:512:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries and households, and that the collateral constraints are state-by-state.
9:302:24155:18:17:98:533:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Here we simply assume that there are only one-period ahead claims and that inter-
9:303:24236:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediaries provide the equipment loans, and only the equipment loans, and must finance
9:304:24321:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these out of their own net worth.  In Section 2.3 we provide an environment with limited
9:305:24409:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enforcement  and  limited  participation  which  is  equivalent  to  the  economy  with  collat-
9:306:24505:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eral  constraints  described  here.   In  that  environment  each  period  has  two  subperiods,
9:307:24601:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:morning and afternoon, and equipment can serve as collateral only in the morning.  The
9:308:24687:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:key assumption affording intermediaries an enforcement advantage is that intermediaries,
9:309:24775:17:18:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but not households, participate in markets at all times; thus, equipment loans must be
9:310:24861:18:18:93:532:109:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:4Holmstr ̈om and Tirole’s (1997) model of financial intermediation also has two implementations – a
9:311:24960:18:0:80:532:91:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:direct one and an indirect one – which are equivalent and they, too, focus on the direct implementation.
10:312:25065:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provided by intermediaries.  Moreover,  limited enforcement of intermediaries’ liabilities
10:313:25155:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that intermediaries must finance such loans out of their own funds.  Thus,  the
10:314:25242:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:properties that we have simply assumed here are in fact endogenous properties of optimal
10:315:25330:17:38:80:177:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic contracts.

12:419:31796:18:15:80:532:92:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and the fact that the firms can never credibly promise their entire net worth in any state next period
12:420:31898:15:0:80:371:77:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(which can be seen by combining (3) at equality with (4) and (5)).
13:421:31966:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borrows the maximum amount it can from both households (at interest rateR) and inter-
13:422:32051:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:B:mediaries (at state-contingent interest rateR′i) as℘i(R′i) = 1−[R−1θ+E[(R′i)−1|z](θi−
13:423:32136:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:θ)](1−δ) (illustrated at the bottom of Figure 1).  Note that the down payment, at times
13:424:32223:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:referred to as the margin requirement, is endogenous in our model.  Using this definition
13:425:32312:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and equations (13) through (15) the firm’s investment Euler equation can then be written
13:426:32400:18:20:80:140:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:concisely as

13:440:32459:28:17:98:533:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The first-order conditions of the intermediary’s problem in equations (7) to (10), which
13:441:32547:17:30:80:315:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are necessary and sufficient, can be written as

13:446:32676:29:17:80:532:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:where  the  multipliers  on  the  constraints  (8)  and  (9)  areμiand  Π(z,z′)βiμ′i,  andηd,

13:448:32857:18:38:80:532:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:dividends and direct and intermediated lending; the envelope condition isvi,w(wi,z) =μi.
13:449:32945:38:25:80:515:354:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.3    Deriving collateral constraints from limited enforcement
13:450:33008:25:17:80:532:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This section describes an economy with limited enforcement which is equivalent to the
13:451:33093:17:18:80:532:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy with collateral constraints described above.  First, we describe the environment
13:452:33181:18:17:80:532:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with limited enforcement; second, we state the equivalent representation with collateral
13:453:33269:17:17:80:532:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraints; and third we sketch our equivalence result which we formally state and prove
13:454:33358:17:18:80:533:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Appendix A.9This equivalence is significant for three reasons;  it shows that (i) the
13:455:33446:18:17:80:532:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restriction to one-period ahead contracts is without loss of generality; (ii) intermediaries
13:456:33538:17:17:80:532:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:must provide equipment loans, that is, loans against the additional amount of collateral
13:457:33626:17:18:80:532:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they  can  seize;  and  (iii)  intermediaries  must  finance  these  loans  out  of  their  own  net
13:458:33726:18:17:80:532:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth.  Thus, the economy with limited enforcement endogenizes three key properties of
13:459:33812:17:17:80:532:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model with collateral constraints that we have simply assumed so far.  That said, a
13:460:33899:17:18:80:532:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reader, who is primarily interested in the dynamic implications of our model, may choose
13:461:33987:18:17:80:370:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to skip this derivation and proceed directly to Section 3.
13:462:34045:17:17:98:533:121:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Suppose that the environment is as before, but that each period has two subperiods
13:463:34127:17:18:80:532:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which we refer to as morning and afternoon.  The economy has limited participation by
13:464:34212:18:0:93:532:86:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:9In Appendix C, we establish this equivalence and characterize the equilibrium in a static environment.
14:465:34317:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:households.  All types of agents participate in markets in the afternoon.  In the morning,
14:466:34407:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however, only entrepreneurs and intermediaries participate in markets but not households.
14:467:34496:18:17:80:483:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is the key assumption affording intermediaries an enforcement advantage.
14:468:34573:17:17:98:533:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The economy has limited enforcement in the spirit of Kehoe and Levine (1993) ex-
14:469:34653:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cept that firms or intermediaries that default cannot be excluded from participating in
14:470:34740:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial and real asset markets going forward.  Rampini and Viswanathan (2010, 2013)
14:471:34825:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:study this class of economies but consider an economy with only one type of lender with
14:472:34912:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deep pockets and hence take the interest rate as given.  We build on their work by con-
14:473:34999:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sidering an economy with two types of lenders, intermediaries and households, of which
14:474:35085:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one has limited net worth, and extend their analysis by determining the interest rates on
14:475:35174:17:18:80:500:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediated finance in dynamic general equilibrium with aggregate fluctuations.
14:476:35255:18:17:98:533:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Specifically, enforcement is limited as follows:  Firms can abscond both in the morning
14:477:35342:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and in the afternoon.  In the morning,  after cash flows are realized,  firms can abscond
14:478:35431:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with  all  cash  flows  and  a  fraction  1−θiof  depreciated  capital,  whereθi∈(0,1).   In
14:479:35523:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the afternoon, firms can abscond with cash flows net of payments made in the morning
14:480:35607:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and a fraction 1−θof depreciated capital, whereθ∈(0,1).  Critically, we assume that
14:481:35690:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:θi> θ,  which  means  that  firms  can  abscond  with  less  capital  in  the  morning  than  in
14:482:35786:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  afternoon.   Intermediaries,  too,  can  abscond  in  both  subperiods,  although  there  is
14:483:35883:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no  temptation  for  intermediaries  to  do  so  in  the  morning,  as  they  will  at  best  receive
14:484:35984:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:payments, and so we can ignore this constraint and focus just on the afternoon.  In the
14:485:36071:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afternoon, intermediaries can abscond with any payments received in the morning.  To
14:486:36155:17:17:80:502:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reiterate, neither firms nor intermediaries are excluded from markets after default.
14:487:36239:17:18:98:533:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The timing is summarized as follows (see Figure 2):  Each afternoon, firms and inter-
14:488:36324:18:17:80:532:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediaries first decide whether to make their promised payments or default.  Then, firms,
14:489:36412:17:17:80:532:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries, and households consume, invest, and borrow and lend.  The next morning,
14:490:36499:17:18:80:532:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash flows are realized.  Firms decide whether to make their promised morning payments
14:491:36585:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or  default.   Firms  carry  over  the  cash  flows  net  of  payments  made  and  intermediaries
14:492:36682:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:carry over any funds received until the afternoon.  No other decisions are made until the
14:493:36771:17:18:80:132:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afternoon.
14:494:36781:18:17:98:533:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is critical that intermediated loans backed by the additional amount of collateral
14:495:36866:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that can be seized in the morning, that is,θi−θ, are in fact repaid in the morning, as by the
14:496:36959:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afternoon firms can abscond with that additional amount of capital and these payments
14:497:37044:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are no longer enforceable.  This implies that these loans are explicitly short term, that is,
14:498:37137:17:17:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are extended in the afternoon and must be repaid in the morning and cannot be rolled
14:499:37221:17:18:80:532:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over.  It moreover implies that these loans must be extended by intermediaries, as only
14:500:37308:18:0:80:532:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they participate in markets in the morning when the claims need to be enforced.  And
15:501:37394:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finally it means that intermediaries must finance these loans out of their own net worth,
15:502:37483:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as they cannot in turn finance them by borrowing from households because they could
15:503:37566:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simply default on promises to repay the households in the afternoon and abscond with
15:504:37650:17:17:80:285:647:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:the payments received in the morning.10
15:505:37689:17:18:98:533:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Financial intermediaries are able to refinance loans that they make to firms up to a
15:506:37773:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fractionθof collateral which are repaid in the afternoon by borrowing from households.
15:507:37859:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In other words, intermediaries’ corporate loans up to fractionθcan be used as collateral
15:508:37947:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to borrow from households,  whereas loans beyond that,  for fractionθi−θ,  have to be
15:509:38032:18:17:80:516:560:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:financed by intermediaries themselves, that is, out of financial intermediary capital.11
15:510:38120:17:17:98:533:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As discussed before, one interpretation of the environment is that there are three types
15:511:38208:17:18:80:533:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of capital, working capital, equipment (fractionθi−θ), and structures (fractionθ) (see
15:512:38294:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 1).  Firms can always abscond with working capital.  Firms cannot abscond with
15:513:38379:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equipment in the morning, but can abscond with equipment in the afternoon.12Firms can
15:514:38464:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:never abscond with structures.  Structure loans can be provided by either intermediaries
15:515:38552:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or households.  In contrast, equipment loans have to be extended by intermediaries, have
15:516:38640:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be repaid in the morning, and have to be finance out of financial intermediary capital.
15:517:38730:17:18:98:533:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For our environment with two subperiods, we can now state the equivalent problem
15:518:38810:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with collateral constraints in sequence form.  Thefirm’s problem(PCC0) at time 0 in the
15:519:38897:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afternoon is to choose a sequencexCC0≡{xCCt}∞t=0wherexCCt= (dt,kt,bt,bit,bat), that is,
15:520:38984:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dividendsdt, capitalkt, state-contingent loans from householdsbt, and state-contingent
15:521:39070:18:18:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:loans from intermediaries to be repaid in the morningbitand in the afternoonbat, given
15:522:39156:18:17:89:532:334:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:10If households were to participate in the morning as well, then they would have the same ability to
15:523:39256:17:15:80:532:317:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:enforce  claims  as  intermediaries,  and  since  households  have  deep  pockets,  there  would  be  no  role  for
15:524:39371:15:14:80:532:302:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:intermediaries at all.  If instead there were only one subperiod and default decisions would have to be
15:525:39474:14:15:80:532:288:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:made simultaneously, and one were to assume that intermediaries nevertheless retained their repossession
15:526:39578:15:14:80:532:273:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:advantage, this would not be sufficient, since intermediaries would have no incentive to default before
15:527:39681:14:14:80:532:259:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:receiving any payments, and intermediaries could finance all corporate loans, including equipment loans,
15:528:39785:14:15:80:532:245:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:with loans from households and hence would not need any intermediary capital; effectively, households
15:529:39886:15:14:80:532:230:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:could use the enforcement ability of the intermediaries fully,  and the economy would be equivalent to
15:530:39988:14:14:80:532:216:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:an economy without subperiods and with only one type of lender,  households,  that can enforce up to
15:531:40088:14:15:80:532:202:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:fractionθi.  Thus, limited participation is essential as a foundation for the economy with two types of
15:532:40191:15:9:80:173:187:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:collateral constraints.
15:533:40214:9:18:89:532:178:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:11In contrast, an intermediary could promise corporate loans backed byθi−θto other intermediaries,
15:534:40312:18:14:80:532:160:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:as these participate in markets in the morning as well, that is, the interbank market is frictionless in our
15:535:40420:14:9:80:445:146:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:model, which is why we are able to consider a representative financial intermediary.
15:536:40504:9:18:89:532:137:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:12The idea is that unlike immovable assets such as structures which are always collateralizable, movable
15:537:40608:18:14:80:532:119:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:assets such as machinery and equipment are bolted down in the morning and hence collateralizable then,
15:538:40710:14:0:80:421:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:but are unbolted by the afternoon and hence can no longer serve as collateral.
16:539:40790:0:37:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worthw0and given the sequence of stochastic interest ratesRi0≡{Rit}∞t=0, to solve

17:608:44475:18:17:98:533:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, let us sketch our main equivalence result (see Appendix A for the formal state-
17:609:44563:17:17:80:532:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment and proof).  The economic intuition for the equivalence of the economy with limited
17:610:44651:17:18:80:532:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enforcement,  described  in  detail  in  Appendix  A,  and  the  economy  with  collateral  con-
17:611:44747:18:17:80:532:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straints discussed in this section is based on two main insights.  First, limited enforcement
17:612:44840:17:17:80:532:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that the present value of any sequence of promises can never exceed the current
17:613:44927:17:18:80:532:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value of collateral, as otherwise delivering on these promises would not be optimal and the
17:614:45018:18:0:80:532:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borrower would default.  Indeed, limited enforcement constraints are equivalent to a type
18:615:45109:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of collateral constraint on the present value of sequences of promises (see Theorem A.1).
18:616:45198:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Second, any sequence of promises satisfying these collateral constraints on present values
18:617:45288:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be implemented with one-period ahead morning and afternoon claims subject to the
18:618:45372:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateral constraints in (25) and (26) for the firm and (31) for the intermediary, respec-
18:619:45463:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tively (see Theorem A.2).  The economy with collateral constraints is tractable, in part
18:620:45551:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because we can hence restrict attention, without loss of generality, to complete markets
18:621:45639:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in one-period ahead morning and afternoon Arrow securities.  An important subtlety in
18:622:45724:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:establishing the equivalence is the determination of the present values of morning and
18:623:45810:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afternoon promises.  The fact that afternoon promises are discounted to the previous af-
18:624:45898:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ternoon by both households and intermediaries at the interest rate charged by households
18:625:45986:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtains by no arbitrage.  Morning promises are discounted to the previous afternoon at
18:626:46072:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the interest rate on intermediated finance, and, if necessary, discounted further back at
18:627:46161:17:17:80:284:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the interest rate charged by households.
18:628:46201:17:18:98:533:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This economy with limited enforcement and limited participation therefore endoge-
18:629:46282:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nizes three key properties that we previously simply assumed in the economy with col-
18:630:46367:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lateral constraints.  Henceforth, we work with the equivalent, recursive formulation of the
18:631:46458:17:44:80:264:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy with collateral constraints.
18:632:46494:44:30:80:428:378:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3    Intermediary capital and steady state
18:633:46536:30:17:80:532:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intermediary capital is scarce in the model.  We first show that, as a consequence, inter-
18:634:46626:17:17:80:532:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediated finance carries a premium and that that premium affects investment and hence
18:635:46711:17:18:80:532:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real economic activity.  We then show that intermediaries are essential in our economy,
18:636:46798:18:17:80:532:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that is, allow the economy to achieve allocations that would not be achievable in their
18:637:46885:17:17:80:532:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:absence.  Finally, we show that in a steady state intermediary finance carries a positive
18:638:46974:17:38:80:532:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spread over direct finance and determine the steady state capitalization of intermediaries.
18:639:47065:38:25:80:326:224:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.1    Cost of intermediated finance
18:640:47101:25:18:80:532:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Internal  funds  and  intermediated  finance  are  both  scarce  in  our  model  and  command
18:641:47194:18:17:80:532:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  premium  as  collateral  constraints  drive  a  wedge  between  the  cost  of  different  types
18:642:47292:17:17:80:532:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of finance.  Since the firm would never be willing to pay more for intermediated finance
18:643:47380:17:18:80:532:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than the shadow cost of internal funds, the premium on internal finance is higher than the

20:693:50657:17:28:80:127:620:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:economy.
20:694:50665:28:17:80:532:592:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The economic intuition is that if intermediary net worth went to zero, the marginal value
20:695:50754:17:17:80:532:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  intermediary  net  worth  in  equilibrium  would  go  to  infinity,  because  intermediaries
20:696:50850:17:18:80:532:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would earn a positive spread forever; as a consequence, intermediaries would never pay
20:697:50936:18:17:80:265:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out all their net worth as dividends.
20:698:50973:17:17:98:533:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since intermediaries always have positive net worth, the interest rate on intermediated
20:699:51060:17:18:80:532:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financeR′imust in equilibrium be such that the representative firm never would want to
20:700:51146:18:17:80:532:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lend  at  that  interest  rate,  as  otherwise  there  would  be  no  demand  for  intermediated
20:701:51242:17:27:80:278:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance, as the following lemma shows:
20:702:51280:27:18:80:532:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Lemma 1.In  any  equilibrium,(i)the  cost  of  intermediated  funds  (weakly)  exceeds  the
20:703:51371:18:17:80:532:426:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:cost of direct finance, that is,R′i≥R;(ii)the multiplier on the collateral constraint for
20:704:51460:17:17:80:532:409:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:direct finance (weakly) exceeds the multiplier on the collateral constraint for intermediated
20:705:51553:17:18:80:532:392:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:finance, that is,λ′≥λ′i; and(iii)the constraint that the representative firm cannot lend
20:706:51641:18:17:80:532:374:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:atR′inever binds, that is,ν′i= 0w.l.o.g.  Moreover, in a deterministic economy,(iv)the
20:707:51727:17:17:80:532:357:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:constraint that the representative intermediary cannot borrow atR′inever binds, that is,
20:708:51815:17:28:80:533:340:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f11:F:η′i= 0; and(v)the collateral constraint for direct financing always binds, that is,λ′>0.
20:709:51903:28:27:98:374:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We define the essentiality of intermediaries as follows:
20:710:51959:27:17:80:532:285:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Definition 3(Essentiality of intermediation).Intermediation isessentialif an alloca-
20:711:52043:17:27:80:434:268:12:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f4:C:tion can be supported with a financial intermediary but not without.15
20:712:52113:27:18:98:533:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The above results together imply that financial intermediaries must always be essen-
20:713:52197:18:17:80:532:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tial.  First note that firms are always borrowing the maximal amount from households,
20:714:52282:17:17:80:532:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:since direct finance is relatively cheap.  If firms moreover always borrow a positive amount
20:715:52374:17:18:80:532:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from intermediaries, then they must achieve an allocation that would not otherwise be
20:716:52459:18:17:80:532:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:feasible.  IfR′i=R, then the firm must be collateral constrained in terms of intermedi-
20:717:52546:17:17:80:532:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ated finance, too, that is, borrow a positive amount.  IfR′i> R, then intermediaries lend
20:718:52635:17:18:80:532:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all their funds to the corporate sector and in equilibrium firms must be borrowing from
20:719:52722:18:18:80:315:119:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries.  We have proved the following:
20:720:52768:18:18:89:532:101:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:15This definition is analogous to the definition of essentiality of money in monetary theory (see, e.g.,
20:721:52872:18:0:80:141:83:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Hahn (1973)).
21:722:52887:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Proposition 3(Essentiality of intermediaries).In an equilibrium in a deterministic econ-
21:723:52975:17:28:80:338:682:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:omy, financial intermediaries are always essential.
21:724:53026:28:38:80:372:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, intermediation always plays a role in our economy.
21:725:53082:38:25:80:507:616:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.3    Intermediary capitalization and spreads in steady state
21:726:53144:25:17:80:532:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In a steady state, intermediary capital is positive and so is the spread on intermediated
21:727:53233:17:28:80:376:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance.  We define a deterministic steady state as follows:
21:728:53293:28:17:80:532:546:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Definition 4(Steady state).A  deterministic  steady  state  equilibrium  is  an  equilibrium
21:729:53385:17:17:80:533:529:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:with constant allocations, that is,x∗≡[d∗,k∗,b′∗,b′∗i,w′∗]andx∗i≡[d∗i,l′∗,l′∗i,w′∗i], and a
21:730:53476:17:28:80:342:512:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:constant interest rate on intermediated financeR′∗i.
21:731:53528:28:17:98:533:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the deterministic steady state, intermediaries are essential, have positive capital,
21:732:53615:17:27:80:207:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and spreads are positive.
21:733:53640:27:17:80:532:440:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Proposition  4(Steady  state).In  a  deterministic  steady  state,  intermediaries  are  es-
21:734:53732:17:18:80:532:423:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:sential, have positive net worth, and pay positive dividends.  The spread on intermediated
21:735:53822:18:17:80:533:405:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:finance isR′∗i−R=β−1i−R >0.Firms borrow the maximal amount from intermediaries.
21:736:53901:17:25:80:365:388:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:The relative (ex dividend) intermediary capitalization is

21:741:53977:17:0:301:340:346:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:?:℘i(β−1i)

21:743:53986:34:17:80:532:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  relative  (ex  dividend)  intermediary  capitalization,  that  is,  the  ratio  of  the  repre-
21:744:54086:17:18:80:532:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sentative intermediary’s net worth (ex dividend) relative to the representative firm’s net
21:745:54176:18:17:80:532:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth (ex dividend), is the ratio of the intermediary’s financing (per unit of capital) to
21:746:54266:17:17:80:532:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the firm’s down payment requirement (per unit of capital).  In a steady state, the shadow
21:747:54355:17:18:80:533:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cost of internal funds of the firm isβ−1−1 while the shadow cost of internal funds of
21:748:54440:18:17:80:532:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  intermediary  isβ−1i−1  and  equals  the  net  interest  rate  on  intermediated  finance
21:749:54534:17:17:80:532:217:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:R′∗i−1.Sinceβi> β, intermediated finance is cheaper than internal funds for firms in
21:750:54618:17:18:80:532:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the steady state, and firms borrow as much as they can from intermediaries.  The spread
21:751:54705:18:17:80:532:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on  intermediated  finance  is  strictly  positive  in  the  steady  state  because  intermediaries
21:752:54804:17:17:80:532:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are less patient than households.  In the analysis of the equilibrium dynamics in the next
21:753:54894:17:18:80:532:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:section  we  find  that  the  spread  on  intermediated  finance  depends  on  the  net  worth  of
21:754:54992:18:17:80:529:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both firms and intermediaries, and can be higher or lower than the steady state spread.
21:755:55079:17:17:98:533:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a steady state equilibrium, financial intermediaries have positive capital and pay
21:756:55164:17:18:80:532:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out  the  steady  state  interest  income  as  dividendsd∗i=  (R′∗i−1)l′∗i.Both  firms  and
21:757:55255:18:0:80:532:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries have positive net worth in the steady state despite the fact that their rates
22:758:55349:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of time preference differ and both are less patient than households.  The reason is that
22:759:55437:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms have access to investment opportunities, but face collateral constraints and hence
22:760:55525:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:need to finance part of their investment internally, and intermediaries can finance part of
22:761:55616:17:17:80:459:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms’ investment more cheaply, but face collateral constraints themselves.
22:762:55691:17:18:98:533:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The determinants of the capital structure of firms and intermediaries are distinct.  In a
22:763:55780:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:steady state, firm leverage, that is, the total value of debt relative to total tangible assets,
22:764:55876:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is 1−℘i(R′∗i) = (R−1θ+(R′∗i)−1(θi−θ))(1−δ) and is determined by the extent to which the
22:765:55963:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm can collateralize tangible assets, as emphasized in Rampini and Viswanathan (2013).
22:766:56051:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast, intermediary leverage can be defined in our indirect implementation as the
22:767:56138:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value of total direct finance divided by the total value of debt, that is,R−1θ(1−δ) divided
22:768:56229:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by (R−1θ+ (R′∗i)−1(θi−θ))(1−δ), which is approximately equal toθ/θi.  Intermediary
22:769:56311:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:leverage  is  therefore  determined  by  the  relative  enforcement  ability  of  households  and
22:770:56408:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries.  The substantial difference in leverage between firms and intermediaries
22:771:56496:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  practice  may  simply  be  a  consequence  of  the  fact  that  their  capital  structures  are
22:772:56595:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determined by different factors.  Thus, the model has the potential to provide consistent
22:773:56684:17:17:80:403:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:guidance on the financial structure of firms and intermediaries.
22:774:56748:17:18:98:533:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Financial intermediaries are essential in our economy.  Intermediated finance is costly
22:775:56835:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the spread on intermediated finance affects investment and aggregate economic out-
22:776:56921:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:put.  Equilibrium determines the capitalization of both firms and intermediaries as well
22:777:57009:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the spread on intermediated finance; in a steady state equilibrium financial interme-
22:778:57097:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diary capital is positive as is the spread on intermediated finance.  Next we consider the
22:779:57187:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics of our economy with intermediated finance, including the dynamics of firm and
22:780:57273:17:45:80:412:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediary net worth and the spread on intermediated finance.
22:781:57336:45:29:80:392:273:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Dynamics of intermediary capital
22:782:57373:29:17:80:532:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our model allows the analysis of the joint dynamics of the capitalization of the corporate
22:783:57463:17:18:80:532:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  intermediary  sector.   The  net  worth  of  firms  and  intermediaries  are  the  key  state
22:784:57561:18:17:80:532:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables determining dynamic intermediated loan demand and supply and the interest
22:785:57644:17:17:80:532:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate on intermediated finance.  The interaction between firms and intermediaries which
22:786:57730:17:18:80:532:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are both subject to financial constraints leads to subtle dynamics with several compelling
22:787:57820:18:17:80:532:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:features.  For example, spreads on intermediated finance are high when both firms’ and
22:788:57906:17:17:80:532:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries’ net worth is low and intermediaries are poorly capitalized even relative
22:789:57994:17:18:80:532:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  firms.   A  key  feature  is  that  intermediary  capital  accumulation  is  slow  relative  to
22:790:58093:18:17:80:532:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate  net  worth  accumulation,  at  least  early  in  a  recovery.   One  reflection  of  this
22:791:58193:17:0:80:532:88:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is that the recovery from a credit crunch, that is, a drop in intermediary net worth, is
23:792:58283:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative slow.  Another reflection is that a simultaneous drop in the net worth of both
23:793:58370:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms  and  intermediaries,  that  is,  a  downturn  associated  with  a  credit  crunch,  results
23:794:58468:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in an especially slow recovery,  and that such recoveries can stall,  with firm investment
23:795:58558:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and output remaining depressed for an extended period of time.  We relate the dynamic
23:796:58643:17:39:80:400:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:properties of our economy to stylized facts in the next section.
23:797:58707:39:25:80:442:591:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Dynamics of intermediary capital and spreads
23:798:58758:25:17:80:532:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Consider  the  recovery  of  the  economy  from  an  initial,  low  level  of  net  worth  of  firms
23:799:58858:17:17:80:532:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and/or intermediaries, say after a downturn or credit crunch, that is, the deterministic
23:800:58946:17:18:80:532:532:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics in an equilibrium converging to the steady state.  We show that the equilibrium
23:801:59034:18:17:80:532:514:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics evolve in two main phases, an initial one in which the corporate sector pays no
23:802:59122:17:17:80:532:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dividends and a second one in which the corporate sector pays dividends.  Intermediaries
23:803:59210:17:18:80:532:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do  not  pay  dividends  until  the  steady  state  is  reached,  except  that  they  may  pay  an
23:804:59308:18:17:80:532:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:initial dividend, if they are initially well capitalized relative to the corporate sector, as
23:805:59401:17:17:80:169:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we discuss below.
23:806:59418:17:18:98:533:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Before stating these results formally (see Proposition 5 below), we provide an intuitive

23:810:59782:18:17:80:532:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms’ collateral constraint on intermediated finance is slack, the intermediated interest

26:961:66825:27:17:98:533:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is worth emphasizing the predictions of our model for the relative speed of adjust-
26:962:66911:17:18:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment of the two endogenous state variables.  In Region ND firm net worth accumulation is
