26:964:67086:17:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more quickly.  Both of these features are in a sense a consequence of the fact that inter-
26:965:67176:17:18:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mediaries accumulate net worth more slowly in our model.  To understand the economic
26:966:67260:18:17:80:532:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intuition  consider  Region  ND  when  both  firms  and  intermediaries  are  constrained  and
26:967:67354:17:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do not pay dividends.  The dynamics of financial intermediary net worth are relatively
26:968:67440:17:18:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple,  since  as  long  as  they  do  not  pay  dividends  (which  is  the  case  until  the  steady
26:969:67542:18:17:80:532:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state is reached),  the intermediaries’ net worth evolves according to the law of motion
26:970:67630:17:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:w′i=R′iwi,that is, intermediary net worth next period is simply intermediary net worth
26:971:67716:17:18:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this period plus interest income.  When no dividends are paid, intermediaries lend out all
26:972:67806:18:17:80:532:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their funds at the (equilibrium) intermediated interest rateR′i,and hence their net worth
26:973:67895:17:17:80:532:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:grows at the (gross) rateR′i.Moreover, the intermediated interest rate is (weakly) less
26:974:67982:17:18:80:532:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than firms’ marginal levered return on capital, which in turn in less than firms’ average
26:975:68071:18:24:80:502:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:levered return on capital which equals the growth rate of firms’ net worth, that is,
26:976:68155:24:16:199:210:241:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f9:?:w′i
26:977:68158:16:0:199:210:225:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f9:?:wi
26:978:68160:0:0:215:252:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:A:=R′i≤
26:979:68165:0:16:257:381:241:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:A′fk(k) + (1−θ)(1−δ)
26:980:68185:16:0:315:322:225:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:℘
26:981:68186:0:0:385:394:233:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:<
26:982:68187:0:16:398:409:241:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f10:?:w′
26:983:68189:16:0:400:408:225:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:w
26:984:68190:0:32:411:414:233:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:.
26:985:68191:32:17:80:532:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is why the net worth of the corporate sector grows faster than the net worth of the
26:986:68279:17:17:80:251:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediary sector in this phase.
26:987:68313:17:18:98:533:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One  reflection  of  this  difference  in  net  worth  growth  is  that  the  corporate  sector
26:988:68408:18:17:80:532:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovers faster, in the sense that firms initiate dividends before intermediaries do.  Once
26:989:68499:17:17:80:532:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms pay dividends (in Region D), it is now the intermediary sector that accumulates net
26:990:68588:17:18:80:532:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth faster as it catches up; so the difference in the growth rate of net worth accumulation
26:991:68681:18:17:80:532:97:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across the two sectors switches sign.  Indeed, as the intermediaries continue to accumulate
26:992:68772:17:0:80:502:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worth, the corporate sector relevers and its net worth may temporarily shrink.
27:993:68856:0:17:98:533:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Below we use this analytical characterization of the dynamic equilibrium to study the
27:994:68941:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics of the economy in response to an initial drop in corporate net worth (a “down-
27:995:69028:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turn”),  an initial drop in the net worth of financial intermediaries (a “credit crunch”),
27:996:69118:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  a  downturn  associated  with  a  credit  crunch,  that  is,  a  simultaneous  drop  in  both
27:997:69216:17:39:80:277:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate and intermediary net worth.
27:998:69253:39:25:80:450:591:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    Dynamics of a downturn without credit crunch
27:999:69304:25:17:80:532:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Suppose the economy experiences a downturn, which we model as an unanticipated one-
27:1000:69387:17:17:80:533:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time drop in corporate net worthw. We consider a downturn without a credit crunch, that
27:1001:69474:17:18:80:532:532:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is,  assume that intermediaries’ net worth remains unchanged at its ex-dividend steady
27:1002:69560:18:17:80:532:514:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state level.  Figure 4 illustrates the dynamics of firm and intermediary net worth, the in-
27:1003:69651:17:17:80:532:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terest rate on intermediated finance, intermediary lending, and investment following such
27:1004:69740:17:18:80:532:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a downturn (at time 0).  In terms of Proposition 5, the recovery evolves in several phases,
27:1005:69831:18:17:80:532:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the net worths of the two sectors transit through various parts of first Region ND and
27:1006:69920:17:17:80:158:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then Region D.
27:1007:69934:17:18:98:533:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:On impact the drop in corporate net worth results in a drop in corporate loan de-
27:1008:70015:18:17:80:532:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mand, leaving intermediaries initially relatively well capitalized.  Indeed, as can be seen in
27:1009:70109:17:17:80:532:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Panel A and Panel B2 of Figure 4, intermediaries respond by paying an initial dividend,
27:1010:70196:17:18:80:532:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as their previous net worth is much more than firms’ reduced loan demand can accom-
27:1011:70279:18:17:80:532:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modate.  Moreover, intermediaries do not pay out all excess funds but conserve some net
27:1012:70366:17:17:80:532:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth to meet future loan demand by lending some of their funds to households; in fact,
27:1013:70453:17:18:80:532:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the intermediaries’ lending to households exceeds their lending to the corporate sector
27:1014:70540:18:17:80:532:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:early on (see Panel B3).  Because intermediaries lend to households at the margin, the
27:1015:70626:17:17:80:532:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium spread on intermediated finance is zero, that is,R′i=R(see Panel B1); in
27:1016:70710:17:18:80:532:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this sense, intermediaries are holding “cash” at an interest rate below their discount rate
27:1017:70801:18:17:80:532:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for some time.  The reason why intermediaries are willing to hold cash at a rate of re-
27:1018:70888:17:17:80:532:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turn below their rate of time preference is because they anticipate an eventual rise in the
27:1019:70979:17:18:80:519:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediated interest rate above their rate of time preference, at least for some time.
27:1020:71067:18:17:98:532:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Intermediaries accumulate net worth at rateRin this phase while the corporate sector
27:1021:71151:17:17:80:532:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accumulates net worth at a faster rate, given the high marginal levered return on capital;
27:1022:71241:17:18:80:532:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus, the net worth of the corporate sector rises relative to the net worth of intermediaries.
27:1023:71335:18:17:80:532:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As firms’ net worth rises, so do corporate investmentk=w/℘i(R) as well as corporate
27:1024:71418:17:17:80:410:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:loan demand.  In Figure 4, this phase last from time 0 to time 4.
27:1025:71483:17:18:98:533:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Eventually, the increased net worth of the corporate sector raises loan demand to the
27:1026:71568:18:17:80:532:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:point  where  intermediated  finance  becomes  scarce  and  the  intermediated  interest  rate
27:1027:71662:17:0:80:532:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rises  (time  5  in  the  figure).   In  the  case  considered  in  Figure  4,  since  the  initial  drop
28:1028:71769:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in net worth is not too large,  it turns out that the cost of intermediated finance stays
28:1029:71858:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:belowβ−1and firms happen to initiate dividend payments at the same time; that is, the
28:1030:71943:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy has reaches Region D at time 5.  Firms’ collateral constraint continues to bind
28:1031:72030:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and, together with firms’ investment Euler equation, jointly determines the intermediated
28:1032:72119:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rate and investment.  Although firms are paying dividends from time 5 onwards,
28:1033:72206:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:neither investment nor intermediaries have fully recovered.  As intermediaries continue to
28:1034:72296:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accumulate net worth between time 5 and time 8, intermediary loan supply increases and
28:1035:72382:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the intermediated interest rate drops.  In response, firms continue to increase investment.
28:1036:72473:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intermediaries’ net worth reaches its (ex dividend) steady state value at time 8 and the
28:1037:72561:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy is back in steady state (as described in Proposition 4) from then on, with the
28:1038:72647:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cost of intermediated finance equal toβ−1i, the unconstrained intermediaries’ shadow cost
28:1039:72736:18:17:80:232:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for providing corporate loans.
28:1040:72766:17:17:98:533:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We emphasize two key aspects of the dynamics of intermediary capital illustrated by
28:1041:72849:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  recovery  from  a  downturn  traced  out  here,  beyond  the  fact  that  intermediary  and
28:1042:72945:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm net worth affect the dynamics jointly.  First, intermediary capital accumulates more
28:1043:73034:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:slowly than corporate net worth as long as both firms and intermediaries are constrained.
28:1044:73123:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Second, when the corporate sector is temporarily relatively poorly capitalized, the interest
28:1045:73215:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate on intermediated finance is low and intermediaries conserve net worth by lending to
28:1046:73303:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:households at a low interest rate to meet the higher subsequent corporate loan demand.
28:1047:73389:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Of course, the second observation is a reflection of the relatively slow pace of intermediary
28:1048:73482:18:38:80:228:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital accumulation as well.
28:1049:73511:38:25:80:317:314:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.3    Dynamics of a credit crunch
28:1050:73545:25:17:80:533:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Suppose the economy experiences acredit  crunch, which we model here as an unantic-
28:1051:73628:17:18:80:532:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ipated  one-time  drop  in  intermediary  net  worthwi.   We  assume  that  the  economy  is
28:1052:73720:18:17:80:532:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:otherwise deterministic and is in steady state when the credit crunch hits with corpo-
28:1053:73806:17:17:80:532:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate net worth at its (ex-dividend) steady state value.  Figure 5 illustrates the effects of
28:1054:73898:17:18:80:532:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such a credit crunch on interest rates, net worth, intermediary lending, and investment.
28:1055:73986:18:17:80:532:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The drop in intermediary net worth results in a reduction in lending and an increase in
28:1056:74073:17:17:80:532:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the spread on intermediated finance on impact (see time 0 in Panel B1).16Moreover, the
28:1057:74159:17:18:80:532:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher cost of intermediated finance increases the user cost of capital (33) as the premium
28:1058:74250:18:17:80:532:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on internal finance increases as well and so the investment Euler equation implies that
28:1059:74337:17:17:80:532:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment drops (see Panel B4).  Hence, a credit crunch has real effects in our model.
28:1060:74424:17:18:80:532:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Due to the limited supply of intermediated finance firms are forced to delever at time 0,
28:1061:74513:18:18:89:532:98:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:16If the credit crunch would hit before dividends are paid, then firms and intermediaries could absorb
28:1062:74615:18:0:80:385:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the shock by cutting dividends, at least partially, reducing its impact.
29:1063:74689:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replacing  reduced  intermediary  loans  with  internal  funds.   Given  their  limited  internal
29:1064:74786:17:18:80:312:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:funds, firms are moreover forced to downsize.
29:1065:74831:18:17:98:533:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:At time 1, the corporate sector reaccumulates net worth leading to an initial partial
29:1066:74916:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovery in investment and output; indeed, firms reinitiate dividend payments at time 1.
29:1067:75004:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However, the economy and especially intermediaries have not fully recovered at this point,
29:1068:75094:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as intermediary net worth remains well below its steady state level.  The recovery stalls,
29:1069:75184:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potentially for a long time (from time 1 to time 14 in Figure 5),  in the sense that the
29:1070:75272:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rate on intermediated finance remains elevated atR′i=β−1> R′∗i=β−1iand
29:1071:75351:18:17:80:533:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment remains constant below its steady state level at ̄k < k∗.  The reason is that
29:1072:75439:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms’ user cost of capital remains elevated despite the fact that the corporate sector is
29:1073:75529:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well  capitalized  and  paying  dividends,  as  intermediaries’  capacity  to  extend  relatively
29:1074:75626:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cheap financing is reduced.  Thus, the real effects in our model are persistent, even if the
29:1075:75718:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate sector recapitalizes relatively quickly, and the full recovery of the real economy
29:1076:75810:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is delayed.  We emphasize that while firms seem to be well capitalized because they are
29:1077:75897:18:17:80:429:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:paying dividends at this point, the economy has not fully recovered.
29:1078:75965:17:17:98:533:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The recovery only resumes once intermediaries accumulate sufficient capital to meet
29:1079:76048:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate loan demand atR′i=β−1.  At that point, intermediary interest rates start to
29:1080:76133:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fall and investment begins to recover (time 15 to 18); as the interest rate on intermediated
29:1081:76225:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance is now below the shadow cost of internal funds of the corporate sector, the collat-
29:1082:76316:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eral constraint binds again.  Investment increases due to the reduced cost of intermediated
29:1083:76407:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing and the recovery resumes.  Eventually (at time 18), intermediaries accumulate
29:1084:76494:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their steady state level of net worth and the cost of intermediated finance reachesβ−1i,
29:1085:76582:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the unconstrained intermediaries’ shadow cost of providing loans, and investment recovers
29:1086:76671:18:17:80:373:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fully; and finally the steady state is reached (at time 19).
29:1087:76731:17:17:98:533:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  emphasize  two  key  additional  aspects  of  the  dynamics  of  our  economy.   First,
29:1088:76822:17:18:80:532:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  recovery  from  a  credit  crunch  can  be  much  delayed,  or  can  stall,  due  to  the  slow
29:1089:76922:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accumulation of intermediary net worth; thus, one feature of a credit crunch in our model
29:1090:77011:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the persistence of the real effects.  Second, the response of firms’ to a credit crunch is
29:1091:77104:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also striking.  In response to a credit crunch, firms cut dividends to substitute retained
29:1092:77194:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings for intermediated loans.  That is, firms delever and temporarily accumulate more
29:1093:77283:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worth than they retain in the steady state, and only as the intermediaries recover, do
29:1094:77373:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms gradually relever.  The interaction between the two sectors which are both subject
29:1095:77461:18:0:80:448:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to financial constraint leads to rich implications for economic dynamics.
30:1096:77536:0:25:80:360:699:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.4    Effects of severity of credit crunch
30:1097:77579:25:17:80:532:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Suppose the economy simultaneously experiences a downturn in corporate net worth and
30:1098:77663:17:18:80:532:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a credit crunch.  Figure 6 illustrates the effect of the severity of the credit crunch itself
30:1099:77756:18:17:80:532:639:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on  the  depth  and  protractedness  of  the  macroeconomic  downturn,  the  joint  dynamics
30:1100:77848:17:17:80:532:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  corporate  and  intermediary  net  worth  accumulation,  and  spreads  on  intermediated
30:1101:77940:17:18:80:532:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance.  We find that downturns associated with a credit crunch are more severe and more
30:1102:78029:18:17:80:515:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:protracted, and feature higher spreads and slower corporate net worth accumulation.
30:1103:78112:17:17:98:533:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 6 traces out three scenarios: a downturn in corporate net worth without a credit
30:1104:78199:17:18:80:532:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crunch (solid), and downturns in corporate net worth associated with a moderate and a
30:1105:78284:18:17:80:532:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:severe credit crunch (dotted and dashed, respectively).  The downturn in corporate net
30:1106:78370:17:17:80:532:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth without a credit crunch is the baseline scenario analyzed in Section 4.1 and Figure 4
30:1107:78461:17:18:80:532:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:above.  As noted there, in this scenario, the intermediary is initially well-capitalized and
30:1108:78553:18:17:80:532:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can hence accommodate the reduced corporate loan demand easily; spreads are initially
30:1109:78638:17:17:80:532:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low, as intermediaries conserve net worth by lending to households.  As corporate loan
30:1110:78724:17:18:80:532:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand  increases  and  the  economy  recovers,  spreads  begin  to  rise  and  eventually  fall
30:1111:78820:18:17:80:532:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:back to the steady state level.  The corporate sector accumulates net worth faster and
30:1112:78906:17:17:80:374:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reinitiates dividends sooner than the intermediary sector.
30:1113:78964:17:18:98:533:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A moderate credit crunch slows the recovery of investment and intermediary lending
30:1114:79046:18:17:80:532:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(see Panel B4 and B3, respectively), and raises spreads earlier and to a higher level (see
30:1115:79136:17:17:80:532:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Panel B1).17Corporate net worth accumulation is also slowed somewhat and the reiniti-
30:1116:79221:17:18:80:532:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ation of corporate dividends is delayed; moreover, the corporate sector first accumulates
30:1117:79310:18:17:80:532:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net  worth,  and  then  partially  draws  down  its  net  worth  as  intermediaries  recover  (see
30:1118:79408:17:17:80:532:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Panel B2).  Moreover,  the recovery stalls,  albeit briefly,  when the corporate sector has
30:1119:79499:17:18:80:532:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovered to the point where it initiates dividends, but the intermediary sector still has
30:1120:79589:18:17:80:532:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not accumulated sufficient net worth to meet loan demand atR′i=β−1(see the leveling
30:1121:79672:17:17:80:532:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:off of investment and spreads from time 6 to 8 in Panels B4 and B1).  Once intermediaries
30:1122:79761:17:18:80:532:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accumulate enough net worth to accommodate loan demand at an interest rate equal to
30:1123:79844:18:18:80:378:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the corporate sector’s discount rate, the recovery resumes.
30:1124:79903:18:18:89:532:205:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:17Indeed,  spreads  rise  over  a  couple  of  periods  (from  time  1  to  time  3);  at  time  2  the  corporate
30:1125:80017:18:14:80:533:187:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:sector borrows all the funds intermediaries are able to lend and investsk= (w+wi)/℘.The interest
30:1126:80113:14:14:80:532:173:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:rate on intermediated finance is determined by the collateral constraint,  which is binding,  and equals
30:1127:80217:14:15:80:532:159:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f6:F:R′i= (θi−θ) (w/wi+ 1) (1−δ)/℘; and since corporate net worth increases faster than intermediary net
30:1128:80316:15:14:80:532:144:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:worth, the interest rate on intermediated finance rises in this phase.  As the corporate sector accumulates
30:1129:80423:14:14:80:532:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:net worth, it can pledge more and the equilibrium interest rate rises.  As the net worth and investment
30:1130:80526:14:15:80:532:116:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of the corporate sector continues to rise faster than intermediary net worth, eventually the increase in
30:1131:80630:15:14:80:532:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:firms’ collateral means that firms’ ability to pledge no longer constrains their ability to raise intermediated
30:1132:80741:14:0:80:278:87:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:finance, at which point spreads start to drop.
31:1133:80789:0:17:98:533:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A severe credit crunch magnifies all these effects, amplifying the downturn, making it
31:1134:80875:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more protracted, leading to longer stalls in the recovery, and raising spreads.  Investment
31:1135:80966:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:initially  drops  more,  and  then  recovers  more  slowly,  stalling  for  an  extend  period  of
31:1136:81064:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time  (time  7  through  16)  before  eventually  recovering  (see  Panel  B4).   The  spread  on
31:1137:81161:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediated finance shoots up on impact, because intermediated finance is limited not
31:1138:81248:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by  corporate  loan  demand  but  by  the  supply  of  intermediated  funds;18the  spread  is
31:1139:81341:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hence determined by the levered marginal product of capital, which is high because the
31:1140:81427:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate sector is financially constrained.19As both sectors accumulate net worth, the
31:1141:81514:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spread comes down from its initial highs, but stalls once the corporate sector starts to
31:1142:81602:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pay  dividends.   Indeed,  the  spread  stays  at  this  elevated  level  while  the  intermediary
31:1143:81700:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sector reaccumulates net worth, and returns to its steady state level only later on (see
31:1144:81788:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Panel  B1).   Intermediary  lending  is  also  noteworthy,  as  it  remains  substantially  below
31:1145:81885:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  steady  state  level  for  an  extended  amount  of  time  (see  Panel  B3).   Finally,  note
31:1146:81983:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  the  corporate  sector  temporarily  accumulates  more  net  worth  than  in  the  steady
31:1147:82078:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state, a result of corporate deleveraging, as firms substitute internal funds for the lack of
31:1148:82171:17:38:80:267:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediated finance for some time.
31:1149:82207:38:25:80:464:401:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.5    Net worth dynamics in bank-dependent economy
31:1150:82258:25:18:80:532:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Suppose now that the economy is more bank dependent; specifically, consider an economy
31:1151:82344:18:17:80:532:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with a higher value ofθi.  Recall from Proposition 4 that this implies that the ratio of
31:1152:82432:17:17:80:532:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediary net worth to corporate net worth in the steady state is higher, that is, a larger
31:1153:82526:17:18:80:532:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fraction of investment is financed by intermediaries.  How does such a bank-dependent
31:1154:82611:18:17:80:532:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy respond to downturns with and without a credit crunch?  The dynamic response
31:1155:82695:17:17:80:532:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of such an economy is illustrated in Figure 7.  To facilitate the comparison, we keep all the
31:1156:82788:17:18:80:532:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameters unchanged from the previous figures, except for two:  first, we raiseθifrom
31:1157:82874:18:17:80:531:254:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:0.8 to 0.9 and second, we reduce the productivityA′to keep steady state investmentk∗
31:1158:82958:17:17:80:532:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unchanged.  Moreover, in a steady statew∗i+w∗=℘k∗, and thus the sum of corporate and
31:1159:83042:17:18:80:532:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediary net worth is unchanged as well, facilitating the comparison.  We consider the
31:1160:83132:18:17:80:532:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:same three scenarios as in Figure 6, a downturn without a credit crunch (solid), as well as
31:1161:83223:17:17:80:532:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:downturns with a moderate and a severe credit crunch (dotted and dashed, respectively).
31:1162:83310:17:18:98:533:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Several  features  of  the  response  are  worth  noting:  First,  the  severity  of  the  credit
31:1163:83407:18:17:80:532:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crunch itself has a more significant impact on the initial drop in investment (see Panel B4).
31:1164:83500:17:18:80:532:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, investment is more substantially reduced both early in the downturn and the
31:1165:83585:18:18:89:532:115:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:18Since intermediaries lend out their entire net worthwito the corporate sector, the law of motion of
31:1166:83686:18:9:80:211:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:investment isk= (w+wi)/℘.
31:1167:83711:9:0:89:532:88:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f14:F:19That is, the equilibrium interest rate on intermediated finance isR′i= [A′fk(k) + (1−θ)(1−δ)]/℘.
32:1168:83811:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recovery stalls at a lower level of investment.  Further,  and perhaps most significantly,
32:1169:83901:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  downturn  is  also  more  protracted  with  investment  reduced,  intermediated  finance
32:1170:83994:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depressed  (see  Panel  B3),  and  spreads  elevated  (see  Panel  B1)  for  longer.   The  effects
32:1171:84093:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on net worth of the two sectors are also magnified:  intermediary net worth takes a long
32:1172:84181:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time to recover and the corporate sector temporarily accumulates substantially more net
32:1173:84268:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth than it has in the steady state, again in an effort to substitute internal funding for
32:1174:84360:17:17:80:329:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the lack of intermediated finance (see Panel B2).
32:1175:84409:17:18:98:533:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our theory predicts that in a bank-dependent economy, downturns associated with a
32:1176:84490:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit crunch are more severe and more protracted, with slower net worth accumulation
32:1177:84575:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and longer stalls of the recovery at lower levels of investment.  Thus, the recovery from
32:1178:84664:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crises in more bank-dependent economies such as Europe or Japan may be substantially
32:1179:84748:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:different from,  and more sluggish than,  that in less bank-dependent economies such as
32:1180:84835:17:38:80:321:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the U.S., where it may be typically more swift.
32:1181:84882:38:25:80:441:453:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.6    Comovement of firm and intermediary capital
32:1182:84932:25:18:80:532:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The focus of our analysis thus far has been on the deterministic dynamics following unan-
32:1183:85021:18:17:80:532:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ticipated drops in net worth. Our model however encompasses economies with uncertainty
32:1184:85107:17:17:80:532:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enabling the analysis of equilibrium risk management of shocks to net worth.  Specifically,
32:1185:85198:17:18:80:532:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we can ask whether we should expect the corporate sector and the intermediary sector to
32:1186:85285:18:17:80:532:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be constrained at the same time, as arguably is the case in downturns associated with a
32:1187:85372:17:17:80:532:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:credit crunch in practice.  In other words, should we expect the net worth (or the marginal
32:1188:85463:17:18:80:380:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value of net worth) of firms and intermediaries to comove?
32:1189:85521:18:17:98:533:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We consider this question in a stochastic economy which is deterministic from time 1
32:1190:85605:17:17:80:532:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:onward.  Importantly, this allows both firms and intermediaries to engage in risk man-
32:1191:85691:17:18:80:531:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:agement at time 0 and hedge the net worth available to them in different statess′∈S
32:1192:85774:18:17:80:532:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at time 1.  We first show that the representative firm optimally engages in incomplete
32:1193:85860:17:17:80:532:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk management, that is, the collateral constraint for direct finance against at least one
32:1194:85951:17:18:80:532:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:states′∈Smust bind.  We then provide sufficient conditions for the marginal value of
32:1195:86035:18:27:80:509:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worth of the representative firm and the representative intermediary to comove.
32:1196:86118:27:17:80:532:175:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Proposition 6(Comovement of the value of firm and intermediary capital).In an econ-
32:1197:86201:17:18:80:533:158:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f21:F:omy that is deterministic from time1onward and has constant expected productivity,(i)
32:1198:86286:18:17:80:532:140:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:the  representative  firm  must  be  collateral  constrained  for  direct  finance  against  at  least
32:1199:86388:17:17:80:532:123:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:one state at time1;(ii)the marginal value of firm and intermediary net worth comove,
32:1200:86472:17:18:80:532:106:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:in  factμ(s′)/μ(s′+) =μi(s′)/μi(s′+),∀s′,s′+∈S,  ifλi(s′) = 0,∀s′∈S.(iii)Suppose
32:1201:86552:18:0:80:532:88:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:moreover that there are just two states, that is,S={ˆs′,ˇs′}.  If only one of the collateral
33:1202:86646:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:F:constraints  for  direct  finance  binds,λ(ˇs′)>0  =λ(ˆs′),  then  the  marginal  values  must
33:1203:86740:17:28:80:292:682:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:comove,μ(ˆs′)> μ(ˇs′)andμi(ˆs′)≥μi(ˇs′).
33:1204:86780:28:17:98:533:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Proposition  6  implies  that  the  marginal  values  of  firm  and  intermediary  net  worth
33:1205:86873:17:17:80:532:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:comove, for example, when the intermediary has very limited net worth and hence the
33:1206:86956:17:18:80:532:620:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateral constraints for intermediated finance are slack for all states.  They also comove
33:1207:87048:18:17:80:532:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if the firm hedges one of two possible states, as then the intermediary effectively must be
33:1208:87139:17:17:80:532:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hedging that state, too.  Thus, the marginal value of intermediary net worth may be high
33:1209:87227:17:18:80:532:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exactly when the marginal value of firm net worth is high, too.  The marginal values may
33:1210:87315:18:17:80:532:550:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however  move  in  opposite  directions,  for  example,  if  a  high  realization  of  productivity
33:1211:87414:17:17:80:532:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:raises  firm  net  worth  substantially,  which  lowers  the  marginal  product  of  capital  and
33:1212:87511:17:18:80:532:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hence the marginal value of firm net worth, while it may raise loan demand substantially
33:1213:87599:18:17:80:397:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and hence raise the marginal value of intermediary net worth.
33:1214:87660:17:17:98:533:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Comovement between the value of corporate and intermediary net worth is thus plau-
33:1215:87742:17:18:80:532:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sible but not a foregone conclusion.  The nature of economic shocks affecting net worth
33:1216:87829:18:17:80:532:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may also play a role.  Throughout we have considered stochastic total factor productivity,
33:1217:87919:17:17:80:532:429:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which  directly  affects  corporate  net  worth  only.   Alternatively,  one  could  easily  adapt
33:1218:88017:17:18:80:532:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model to consider stochastic depreciation of capital, which would directly affect both
33:1219:88107:18:17:80:532:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corporate and intermediary net worth; in fact, stochastic depreciation shocks would ar-
33:1220:88194:17:17:80:532:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:guably affect intermediary net worth relatively more, as the assets of intermediaries are
33:1221:88283:17:18:80:532:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateralized claims.  Depreciation shocks are one way to model shocks to the value of
33:1222:88370:18:17:80:532:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateral.  A shock to total factor productivity may then result in a downturn without
33:1223:88457:17:17:80:532:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  credit  crunch,  whereas  a  depreciation  shock  to  the  value  of  capital  may  result  in  a
33:1224:88557:17:18:80:532:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:downturn associated with a credit crunch.  We leave an explicit analysis of a model with
33:1225:88645:18:44:80:449:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both stochastic productivity and stochastic depreciation to future work.
33:1226:88717:44:29:80:458:246:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5    Revisiting evidence on crises with theory
33:1227:88763:29:17:80:532:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our model provides guidance on the joint dynamics of the macro economy and the fi-
33:1228:88845:17:18:80:532:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nancial  sector.   We  use  the  model  and  the  analysis  of  the  net  worth  dynamics  in  the
33:1229:88943:18:17:80:532:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previous section to revisit three main stylized facts about downturns associated with fi-
33:1230:89032:17:17:80:532:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nancial crises, namely their severity, their protractedness, and the relation between the
33:1231:89121:17:0:80:515:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:severity of the financial crisis itself and the severity and persistence of the downturn.
34:1232:89212:0:25:80:535:699:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:5.1    Fact 1: Severity of downturns associated with financial crises
34:1233:89281:25:17:80:532:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Prior empirical research shows that downturns associated with financial crises are more
34:1234:89368:17:18:80:532:657:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:severe.   Reinhart  and  Rogoff  (2014)  find  that  “the  average  peak-to-trough  decline  for
34:1235:89464:18:17:80:532:639:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  US  real  per  capita  GDP  across  nine  major  crises  is  about  9  percent.”   Similarly,
34:1236:89562:17:17:80:532:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using panel data for a large set of countries, Cerra and Saxena (2008) find that “banking
34:1237:89651:17:18:80:532:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crises  lead  to  severe  output  loss  [even  in  high-income  countries]”  (page  442).   Finally,
34:1238:89751:18:17:80:532:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Krishnamurthy and Muir (2016) conclude that “[o]ur results affirm  that financial crises
34:1239:89839:17:17:80:408:570:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:do result in deeper and more protracted recessions” (page 15).20
34:1240:89903:17:18:98:533:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Thus, the evidence shows a first stylized fact, namely that downturns associated with
34:1241:89988:18:17:80:532:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial  crises  are  more  severe  in  the  sense  that  output  losses  are  larger,  suggesting
34:1242:90088:17:17:80:532:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:amplification of macroeconomic shocks.  The evidence also shows that such downturns
34:1243:90171:17:18:80:532:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  more  severe  in  the  sense  of  being  more  protracted,  but  while  these  two  notions  of
34:1244:90271:18:17:80:532:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:severity are often commingled in the literature, we treat their persistence as a separate
34:1245:90360:17:17:80:532:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stylized fact which we discuss in the next subsection.  Comparing the dynamics of our
34:1246:90445:17:18:80:532:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model  without  and  with  a  credit  crunch  in  Figures  4  and  6,  we  find  that  downturns
34:1247:90541:18:17:80:532:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:associated with a financial crisis are more severe, in the sense that output drops by more
34:1248:90631:17:17:80:532:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on impact and that output is lower at any fixed horizon.  That said, the initial effect of
34:1249:90721:17:18:80:532:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the credit crunch on output can be muted in the model if the drop in corporate net worth
34:1250:90809:18:17:80:532:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduces loan demand so much that loan demand drops below (ex-dividend) intermediary
34:1251:90892:17:38:80:133:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worth.
34:1252:90902:38:25:80:425:324:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.2    Fact 2:  Slow recoveries after financial crises
34:1253:90956:25:18:80:532:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The evidence also shows that recoveries after financial crises are protracted.  Reinhart and
34:1254:91048:18:17:80:532:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rogoff (2014) state that “a significant part of the costs of [systemic banking] crises lies in
34:1255:91142:17:17:80:532:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the protracted and halting nature of the recovery” (page 50).  Moreover, they argue that
34:1256:91230:17:19:80:532:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:”[t]he halting, tentative nature of the post-crisis recoveries (even in cases where there is a
34:1257:91324:19:18:89:532:228:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:20We recognize that the conclusions regarding these stylized facts in part turn on the assumptions made
34:1258:91427:18:14:80:532:210:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:for measurement, for example, the severity cutoff used in defining a crisis, the definition of a recovery
34:1259:91532:14:15:80:532:196:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:(return to the previous output level or trend), adjustment for population growth, the definition of the
34:1260:91635:15:14:80:532:181:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:start of the episode (previous output peak or start of the financial disruption), and finally whether the
34:1261:91740:14:14:80:532:167:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:data includes emerging economies and pre-war episodes.  Indeed, some recent studies provide a contrarian
34:1262:91844:14:15:80:532:153:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:view.  For example, Bordo and Haubrich (2012) find “generally . . . rapid recoveries” with the exception of
34:1263:91951:15:14:80:532:138:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the 1930s, 1990s, and the present recovery.  Similarly, Romer and Romer (2015) find that “output declines
34:1264:92056:14:14:80:532:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:following financial crises in modern advanced countries are highly variable, on average only moderate,
34:1265:92158:14:15:80:532:110:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:and often temporary,” (abstract) using a new, qualitative measure of financial distress with a relatively
34:1266:92263:15:14:80:532:95:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:fine scale, thus, challenging the conventional wisdom that “the aftermath of financial crises is typically
34:1267:92369:14:0:80:487:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:severe and long-lasting” (page 1).  We match the stylized facts that are the mainstream view.
35:1268:92464:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sharp—but not sustained—growth rebound) is evidenced in the relatively high incidence
35:1269:92549:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of double dips (or secondary downturns before the previous peak is reached)” (page 52).
35:1270:92636:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:They  find  that  “[o]n  average  it  takes  about  eight  years  to  reach  the  pre-crisis  level  of
35:1271:92739:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:income,” with a median time of about 6.5 years, and that about 45% of the 100 crises
35:1272:92823:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they study are associated with a double dip, and about two-thirds of the most severe crises
35:1273:92914:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:involve double-dips.  Cerra and Saxena (2008) find “that the large output loss associated
35:1274:93003:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with financial crises ... is highly persistent” (page 456); specifically, they show that the
35:1275:93095:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:output loss on impact of a banking crisis is about 7.5 percent and the output loss at a
35:1276:93182:18:17:80:423:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ten-year horizon exceeds 6 percent, that is, is extremely persistent.
35:1277:93251:17:17:98:533:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our second stylized fact is therefore the persistence of downturns associated with fi-
35:1278:93337:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nancial crises; recoveries are slow and frequently stall, at least temporarily.  The dynamics
35:1279:93430:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of our model in Figure 5 highlight the protractedness of a credit crunch:  the recovery
35:1280:93517:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of output after a credit crunch is slower than after a regular downturn (compare to Fig-
35:1281:93605:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ure 4).  In addition, spreads remain elevated for an extended period of time.  This is due
35:1282:93695:18:17:80:429:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the relative sluggishness of intermediary net worth accumulation.
35:1283:93763:17:17:98:533:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Moreover, when both corporate and intermediary net worth drop at the same time,
35:1284:93842:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that is,  in a downturn associated with a credit crunch,  downturns are more prolonged
35:1285:93928:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(see  Figure  6)  and  the  recovery  can  stall,  potentially  for  an  extended  period  of  time,
35:1286:94028:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:due to the joint dynamics of corporate and intermediary net worth; note that such stalls
35:1287:94116:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can occur even in cases in which the initial rebound of output is quite brisk, consistent
35:1288:94205:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the data.  The model therefore captures what Reinhart and Rogoff call the “halting,
35:1289:94293:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tentative nature” of such recoveries.  We are not aware of other models that predict such
35:1290:94382:17:39:80:297:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stalls in the economic recovery post crises.
35:1291:94426:39:25:80:426:279:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.3    Fact 3:  Impact of severity of financial crises
35:1292:94480:25:17:80:532:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Further,  the  evidence  suggests  that  how  severe  the  financial  crises  per  se  is  plays  an
35:1293:94580:17:17:80:532:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:important role.  Romer and Romer (2015) find that “one factor that appears to be im-
35:1294:94664:17:18:80:532:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portant to the variation [in the aftermath of crises] is the severity and persistence of the
35:1295:94756:18:17:80:532:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crisis itself” (page 41).  For example, “Japan’s dismal economic performance ...  [may be]
35:1296:94846:17:17:80:532:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related to the fact that the distress was particularly severe and long-lasting” (page 38),
35:1297:94936:17:18:80:532:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and for the 2008 Crisis they argue that “the extreme nature of the recent distress is one
35:1298:95025:18:17:80:532:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likely reason for the severe and continuing economic weakness” (page 41-42).  In a similar
35:1299:95115:17:17:80:532:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spirit, Krishnamurthy and Muir (2016) measure the severity of a crisis using the spread
35:1300:95202:17:18:80:532:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between high-yield and low-yield bonds, and conclude that “recessions in the aftermath
35:1301:95288:18:17:80:532:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of financial crises are severe and protracted” and that furthermore “the severity of the
35:1302:95376:17:0:80:503:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subsequent crisis can be forecast by the size of [changes in the spread]” (abstract).
36:1303:95463:0:17:98:533:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Thus, the third stylized fact is that the severity of the financial crises itself in turn
36:1304:95552:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affects  both  the  severity  and  protractedness  of  the  downturn;  in  other  words,  Fact  1
36:1305:95649:18:17:80:532:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(“severity”) and Fact 2 (“protractedness”) are a matter of degree.  Our model captures
36:1306:95735:17:17:80:532:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this fact as demonstrated in Figure 6: the more severe the drop in intermediary net worth,
36:1307:95825:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the larger the drop in output and the more protracted the recovery;  indeed,  recoveries
36:1308:95913:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from severe financial crises are more protracted in the sense that (i) the initial recovery
36:1309:96004:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is slower, (ii) the recovery stalls for longer, and (iii) the economy takes longer to recover
36:1310:96097:17:18:80:105:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fully.
36:1311:96103:18:17:98:533:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The dynamics of spreads also have empirically plausible features:  spreads “blow out”
36:1312:96188:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when the financial crisis is more severe, recover relatively quickly initially, but then re-
36:1313:96280:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:main  elevated  and  recover  fully  only  after  an  extended  period  of  time.   For  spreads,
36:1314:96377:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Krishnamurthy and Muir (2016) find that “the start of a crisis is associated with a spike
36:1315:96466:17:17:80:532:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  spreads”  and  “a  spike  in  spreads  shifts  down  the  conditional  distribution  of  output
36:1316:96565:17:18:80:532:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth,  fattening the lower tail” (page 17).  Our model captures these observations in
36:1317:96652:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two ways:  first, more severe downturns are associated with higher spreads, and, second,
36:1318:96740:17:17:80:343:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spreads spike at the beginning of very severe crises.
36:1319:96793:17:18:98:533:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The measurement in the aforementioned studies is predicated on the assumption that
36:1320:96875:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there are two separate driving forces, one for downturns and one for financial crises.  Con-
36:1321:96967:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sidering the effects of a credit crunch or financial crisis on aggregate dynamics implicitly
36:1322:97059:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumes that the financial disruption is a separate, exogenous force, rather than simply
36:1323:97147:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an endogenous reflection of a single aggregate source of fluctuations.  Understanding these
36:1324:97238:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:facts therefore calls for a model with two state variables, one for the corporate sector and
36:1325:97330:17:45:80:469:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one for financial intermediaries, which is the type of model that we provide.
36:1326:97407:45:29:80:202:273:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:6    Conclusion
36:1327:97422:29:17:80:532:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We develop a dynamic theory of financial intermediation and show that the capital of
36:1328:97506:17:18:80:532:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both the financial intermediary and corporate sector affect real economic activity, such
36:1329:97594:18:17:80:532:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as firm investment, financing, and the spread between intermediated and direct finance.
36:1330:97681:17:17:80:532:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We derive collateral constraints from an explicit model of limited enforcement in which
36:1331:97768:17:18:80:532:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial intermediaries have a collateralization advantage due to limited participation by
36:1332:97859:18:17:80:532:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:households.  Financial intermediaries participate in markets at all times allowing them to
36:1333:97949:17:17:80:532:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enforce claims when more of the capital is collateralizable.  This advantage in enforcement
36:1334:98040:17:18:80:532:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enables financial intermediaries to lend more than households, but they cannot in turn
36:1335:98126:18:17:80:532:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finance such loans by borrowing from households and hence have to finance these loans
36:1336:98211:17:0:80:532:88:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out of their own net worth; we argue that this is why financial intermediaries need capital.
37:1337:98305:0:17:80:532:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our view, the enforcement of payment is a key rationale for the existence of financial
37:1338:98394:17:18:80:532:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries, in addition to the monitoring and liquidity provision motives emphasized
37:1339:98482:18:17:80:211:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the previous literature.
37:1340:98509:17:17:98:533:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  determinants  of  capital  structure  of  firms  and  intermediaries  in  the  model  are
37:1341:98603:17:18:80:532:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distinct.  Firms’ capital structure is determined by the extent to which firms can pledge
37:1342:98692:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their  tangible  assets  required  for  production  as  collateral  to  intermediaries  and  house-
37:1343:98791:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:holds.  In contrast, intermediaries’ capital structure is determined by the extent to which
37:1344:98882:17:18:80:532:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their collateralized loans can be collateralized themselves, that is, by the difference be-
37:1345:98973:18:17:80:532:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tween the intermediaries’ and households’ ability to collateralize claims.  In other words,
37:1346:99064:17:17:80:532:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms issue promises against tangible assets whereas intermediaries issue promises against
37:1347:99154:17:18:80:532:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:collateralized claims, which are in turn backed by tangible assets.  Thus, given these dis-
37:1348:99245:18:17:80:532:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinct determinants, firm leverage may be substantially lower than intermediary leverage
37:1349:99332:17:17:80:208:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as is the case in practice.
37:1350:99359:17:18:98:533:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Central  to  the  aggregate  implications  is  the  fact  that  our  model  features  two  state
37:1351:99455:18:17:80:532:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables, the net worth of the corporate and intermediary sector.  It is the joint dynamics
37:1352:99547:17:17:80:532:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  these  two  state  variables  that  result  in  the  compelling  dynamics  of  the  model.   In
37:1353:99646:17:18:80:532:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:downturns associated with a credit crunch, while the initial recovery can be quite brisk,
37:1354:99735:18:17:80:532:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the recovery can stall as the intermediary sector is more slow to recover; thus, investment
37:1355:99826:17:17:80:532:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and macroeconomic activity may remain depressed, and spreads elevated, potentially for
37:1356:99912:17:18:80:532:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  prolonged  period  of  time,  even  if  the  corporate  sector  seems  to  have  recovered  and
37:1357:100010:18:17:80:532:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pays dividends.  In a downturn without a credit crunch, corporate loan demand falls, and
37:1358:100098:17:17:80:532:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediaries  may  hold  cash  to  meet  future  corporate  loan  demand  and  thus  spreads
37:1359:100192:17:18:80:532:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may  initially  be  very  low.   A  key  factor  driving  these  results  is  that  intermediary  net
37:1360:100293:18:17:80:445:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth accumulates more slowly than corporate net worth in the model.
37:1361:100361:17:17:98:533:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our model is consistent with three key stylized facts about macroeconomic downturns
37:1362:100444:17:18:80:532:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:associated with a credit crunch, namely, their severity, their protractedness, and the fact
37:1363:100535:18:17:80:532:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the severity of the credit crunch itself in turn affects the severity and the persistence
37:1364:100629:17:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  downturn.   Most  uniquely,  our  model  captures  the  tentative  and  halting  nature
37:1365:100725:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of recoveries from such episodes, a fact emphasized by Reinhart and Rogoff (2014).  Our
37:1366:100812:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model provides a useful framework for the analysis of the dynamic interaction between
37:1367:100897:17:0:80:291:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial structure and economic activity.

47:1764:119879:18:17:80:532:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the former case we can shift the payment to the afternoon and (C.16) holds without loss
47:1765:119969:17:17:80:532:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of generality.  This establishes the equivalence of the economy with limited enforcement

65:2464:153132:29:17:80:532:670:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In this appendix we study how the choice between intermediated and direct finance varies
65:2465:153220:17:18:80:532:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with firm and intermediary net worth in a static (one period) version of our model with a
65:2466:153309:18:17:80:532:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:representative firm.  We further simplify by considering the deterministic case, although

65:2470:153662:17:38:80:525:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intermediated and direct finance in the cross section of firms with different net worths.

69:2615:162308:38:25:80:478:256:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:Appendix C.2:  Effect of intermediary capital on spreads
69:2616:162364:25:17:80:532:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The equilibrium spread on intermediated finance depends on both firm and intermedi-
69:2617:162447:17:18:80:532:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ary net worth.  Given firm net worth, spreads are higher when the intermediary is less
69:2618:162533:18:17:80:532:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well capitalized.  Importantly, the spread on intermediated finance depends on the rela-
69:2619:162621:17:17:80:532:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive capitalization of firms and intermediaries.  Spreads are particularly high when firms
69:2620:162711:17:18:80:532:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  poorly  capitalized  and  intermediaries  are  relatively  poorly  capitalized  at  the  same
69:2621:162809:18:17:80:532:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time.  Poor capitalization of the corporate sector does not per se imply high spreads, as
69:2622:162898:17:17:80:532:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms’  limited  ability  to  pledge  may  result  in  a  reduction  in  firms’  loan  demand  which
69:2623:162998:17:17:80:431:110:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:intermediaries with given net worth can more easily accommodate.22

75:2820:176719:0:41:323:532:738:12:g_d0_f46:12:g_d0_f46:?:Appendix -- For Online Publication
75:2821:176753:41:18:98:533:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Intermediated finance is costlier than direct finance.  Indeed, under the conditions of
75:2822:176840:18:17:80:532:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the proposition, intermediated finance is costlier than the shadow cost of internal finance
75:2823:176931:17:17:80:532:662:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of well capitalized firms.  Thus, well capitalized firms, which pay dividends, do not borrow
75:2824:177023:17:18:80:532:645:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from financial intermediaries.  In contrast, firms with net worth belowwuhave a shadow
75:2825:177109:18:17:80:532:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cost of internal finance which is sufficiently high that they choose to borrow a positive
75:2826:177198:17:17:80:532:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:amount  from  intermediaries.   For  severely  constrained  firms,  with  net  worth  belowwl,
75:2827:177292:17:18:80:532:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  shadow  cost  of  internal  funds  is  so  high  that  they  borrow  as  much  as  they  can
75:2828:177389:18:17:80:532:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from intermediaries,  that is,  their collateral constraint for intermediated finance binds.
75:2829:177481:17:17:80:487:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, more constrained firms have lower investment and are hence smaller.
75:2830:177558:17:18:98:533:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  cross-sectional  capital  structure  implications  are  plausible:   smaller  and  more
75:2831:177650:18:17:80:532:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constrained  firms  borrow  more  from  financial  intermediaries  and  have  higher  costs  of
75:2832:177745:17:17:80:532:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing, while larger and less constrained firms borrow from households, for example in
75:2833:177834:17:444:80:316:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bond markets, and have lower financing costs.
